  • рдХрдердВ рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕реНрдирд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╢реМрдЪрд╛рд░реНрдерддрд╛ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдпрддреЗ ред рди рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕реНрдирд╛рддрдГ рд╢реБрдЪрд┐рд╢реН рдЪреЛрднрдпрд╡рд┐рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреЛ рджреЗрд╡рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреЗ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреБрдЬреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╕реНрдирд╛рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╢реБрдЪрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рддреН, рдХреГрддрд╢реМрдЪрд╛рдЪрдордирд╛рджреЗрдГ рд╕реНрдирд╛рдирд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рдирд╛рддреН, “рд╕реНрдирд╛рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЪрд╛рдЪрд╛рдиреНрддрдГ рдкреБрдирд░реН рдЖрдЪрд╛рдореЗрддреН” (рд╡рдзреН рей.рейрео) рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪ рд╕реНрдирд╛рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкрд┐ рд╢реБрдЪрд┐рд░реН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдПрддрд╛рд╡рддрд╛ рдпрд╛рджреГрд╢реА рд╕реБрджреНрдзрд┐рд╕реН рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд╕реНрдирд╛рдирдореН рдЕрдкрд┐ рд╕рддрд┐ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдВ рдкреБрдирд░реН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╕реНрдореГрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рдВ рдЪреЗрджрдореН рдЕрд╕рддреНрдпреН27 рдЕрд╢реБрдЪрд┐рддреНрд╡реЗ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддреЗ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрд╛рд░реНрдердореН ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ “рд╡реЗрджрдореН рдЕрдзреАрддреНрдп рд╕реНрдирд╛рдпрд╛рддреН” (рдмреМрдЧреН реи.рел.рем) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддреЗ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╡рд┐рдзреМ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╕рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдпрддрд┐ ред

рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдордГ (рдЪреНреЬреНред рдореНрдзреН реи.резреореп) ред

  • рд╕рдорд┐рджрд╛рдзрд╛рдирдВ рд╕рд╛рдпрдореНрдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд░реН рдЕрдЧреНрдиреМ рджрд╛рд░реБрд╢рдХрд▓рдкреНрд░рдХреНрд╖реЗрдкрдгрдореН рее реи.резренрем рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

Everyday, тАШhaving bathed and become pure,тАЩтАФi.e., having his uncleanliness removed by bath,тАФтАШhe should make offerings to Deities, Sages and Fathers.тАЩ If he is already clean, he need not bathe; as the adding of the term тАШcleanтАЩ clearly shows that the тАШbathingтАЩ here laid down is only for the purpose of cleanliness, and hence its performance is absolutely compulsory, like the тАШbathingтАЩ to be done by the Sn─Бlaka, Accomplished Student. It is for this reason that in another Smс╣Ыti bathing has been prohibited (for the Religious Student); though this prohibition refers to bathing with clay, for purposes of personal adornment. Gautama however has prescribed actual bathing. Hence what is meant is that one should plunge into water like a stick, and he should remove dirt, etc., by rubbing the body with his hauds. Unless there is touching of an unolean thing, such dirt as arises from perspiration, or from contact with the dust contained in the clothing, etc., does not make one тАШuncleanтАЩ; for the presence of such dirt is inevitable. Says the Br─Бhmaс╣ЗaтАФтАШWhat is dirt? Is it the skin, or hairs of the beard or penance?тАЩтАФwhich shows that the presence of such тАШdirtтАЩ is conducive to spiritual merit.

тАЬHow is it known that the bathing (here laid down) is for the purposes of cleanliness?тАЭ

The present injunction cannot be taken as prompting, to the performance of divine service, a person who fulfills the two distinct qualifications of тАШhaving bathedтАЩ and тАШbecome cleanтАЩ;

(1) because as a matter of fact, one who has bathed can never remain unclean;

(2) because even for a person who has adopted cleanliness by having sipped water, etc., bathing is found to be enjoined;

(3) because we meet with such passages as тАШhaving bathed, sipped water, one should sip water again,тАЩ where even for the person who has bathed a method of further cleanliness is enjoined.

From all this it is clear that what the present verse enjoins is that whenever occasion (in the shape of the contact of unclean things, etc.) arises, one should bathe, even though there be already present the тАШcleanlinessтАЩ that is generally understood as such.

Or, the present verse may be regarded as a totally independent rule, intended to prohibit bathing without special occasion arising in the shape of uncleanliness; and it is iu view of this, prohibition that we have the counter-exceptionтАФтАШone should bathe after having learnt the Veda,тАЩтАФwhich enjoins bathing at the end of Vedic Study (even in the absence of any uncleanlincss).

тАЬHe should make offerings to Deities, Sages and Fathers.тАЭтАФBy reason of the mention of тАШtarpaс╣Зa,тАЩ the тАШofferingтАЩ here meant appears to be that offering of water to the Deities and others which has been prescribed among the duties of the house-holder, under 3.283. The authors of Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtras also have declared this act as to be done, with water only; e.g., says ─А┼Ыval─Бyana (3.1.3)тАФтАШHe satisfies the Deities.тАЩ Inordinary life also this act is known as the тАШoffering of water.тАЩ

The Deities to whom this offering is to be made have been enumerated by the writers on Gс╣ЫhyaтАФvis., Agni, Praj─Бpati, Brahm─Б and so forth. The тАШtarpaс╣Зa,тАЩ тАШoffering,тАЩ to these does not consist of producing in them the feeling of satisfaction (which is the etymological meaning of the term тАШtarpaс╣ЗaтАЩ); it consists only in the pouring, on their behalf, of water with joined hands. Hence what is here laid down comes to be only a sacrificial offering, in which water is the substance offered. Specially as the character of тАШdeityтАЩ could not otherwise have belonged to those to whom the offering is made; for that alone has been called тАШdeityтАЩ to whom a sacrifice is offered; it is not one who becomes satisfied. The only definition of тАШdeityтАЩ that we have isтАФтАШDeities are recipients of hymns and recipients of offeringsтАЩ; they become тАШrecipients of hymnsтАЩ by becoming the objects of eulogy, and they become тАШrecipients of offeringsтАЩ by becoming those to whom offerings are made. When therefore our author speaks of them as тАШtarpya,тАЩ тАШto be satisfied,тАЩ he uses the term in its figurative sense of тАШbeing recipients of the offering of water.тАЩ The teacher and such other persons are recognised as тАШrecipientsтАЩ when the cow and such things are transferred to their ownership; and the Deities also are тАШrecipients.тАЩ Thus both having the common character of тАШbeing recipients,тАЩ they are described as тАШbeing satisfied.тАЩ If what is laid down here meant actual тАШsatisfyingтАЩ of the Deities, then this^(:) water-offeringтАЩ would become a purely sanctificatory act; and yet no тАШSanctificationтАЩ is possible in the case of Deities; for the simple reason that they have not been, nor are they ever likely to lie, employed; and what has never been employed, or is not likely to be employed, cannot rightly be regarded as an object of sanctification.

тАШSages,тАЩтАФi.e., those sages that happen to be oneтАЩs тАШGotra-с╣Ыс╣гisтАЩ; e.g., for those belonging to the тАШPar─Б┼Ыara-gotra,тАЩ Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha, ┼Ъakti and P─Бr─Б┼Ыarya would be the тАШsagesтАЩ (to whom the offering is to be made). The author of Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtras have however spoken of the тАШseers of Vedic MantrasтАЩ (and not the Gotra-с╣Ыс╣гis) as the тАШsagesтАЩ to whom the offering is to be made; i.e., the sages Madhucchandas, Gс╣Ыtsamada and Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra. Since the text speaks of тАШsagesтАЩ without any qualification, it is open to us to take it as standing for both kinds of sages; but in view of the fact that the Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtras have specified them (as being the тАШseers of mantrasтАЩ), it is only right to take these latter as meant.

тАШFathers.тАЩтАФOneтАЩs dead ancestors,тАФfather, grandfather, etc., all Sapiс╣Зс╕Нas and Sam─Бnodakas. In the case of the тАШFathers,тАЩ the тАШofferingтАЩ is to be the actual тАШTarpaс╣ЗaтАЩ itself. This is going to be distinctly laid down under the rules bearing upon ┼Ъr─Бddha.

Worshiping of the Deities.тАФIn connection with this some ancient writers have made the following observations:тАФтАЬWho are these deities, whose тАШworshipтАЩ is here laid down? If they are meant to be those pninted in picture-booksтАФfigures with four arms, with a thunderbolt in the hand and so forth,тАФthen, since ordinary men regard these as тАШimagesтАЩ (which connotes unreality), they can be called тАШDeity,тАЩ only figuratively. If, on the other hand, they are meant to be those related to hymns and offerings,тАФwhich are indicated by Vedic injunctions, and also by the words of mantras, and which are called so by persons versed in the use of words and their denotations,тАФsuch as тАШAgni,тАЩ тАШAgni-Soma,тАЩ тАШMitra-Varuс╣Зa,тАЩ тАШIndra,тАЩ тАШViс╣гс╣Зu,тАЩ and so forthтАФthen, in that case, their character of тАШDeity,тАЩ would be dependent upon the said acts (of offering, etc.), and not upon the fact of their having any connection with the denotation (of the term тАШDeityтАЩ); and further, a particular (Deity) would be the тАШDeityтАЩ for only that offering which is enjoined as to be offered to him; e.g., when the тАШCake baked upon eight pans,тАЩ is called тАШ─БgneyaтАЩ (dedicated to Agni), Agni becomes the тАШdeityтАЩ only of that cake, and not of that which is called тАШsauryaтАЩ (dedicated to S┼лrya).тАЭ

From the above considerations the conclusion that the ancient writers have deduced is as follows:тАФIn cases where the term cannot be. taken in its direct denotation, it is only right to take it in the figurative sense; specially as such is the actual usage. Hence the тАШworshipтАЩ enjoined in the present verse is that of images.

What the truth on this point is we shall explain below, under verse 189.

тАШPlacing of fuelтАЩтАФthrowing into the fire pieces of wood, every morning and evening.тАФ(176)

  • рдирдиреБ рдЪ рдиреАрд░рд╕рд╕реНрдп рднреЛрдЬреНрдпрддреНрд╡рд╛рд╕рдВрдмрд╡рд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рд░реН рдПрд╡ рди рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рд╕рддреНрдпрдореН ред рдЙрджреНрд░рд┐рдХреНрддрд░рд╕рд╛рдГ рдХреЗрд╡рд▓рд╛ рдЧреБрдбрд╛рджрдпреЛ рдирд┐рд╖рд┐рдзреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░рдХрд░рдгреЗ рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд░реНрдЧрддрд╛рдирд╛рдореН рдЕрдкрд┐ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрдГ ред рдЕрде рд╡рд╛рддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рд╕рд┐рдирдГ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХреГрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдиреНрдирд╕реНрдп рд╕рдХреНрддрд┐рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЛ34 рд╜рдпрдореН ред рдпрдереЛрдХреНрддрдореН-

  • рдпреЗ рддреНрд╡реН рдПрд╡рдВ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЪрдХреНрд╖рддреЗ рд╢реБрдХреНрддрд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рд░рд╕рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╢рдмреНрджреЗрдирд╛рдорд╛рдирд╕рд╛рдирд┐38 рд╡рдЪрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐, рдд рдЗрджрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ ред рдЕрд░реНрдердкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдВ рдХрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рди рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рд╕рддрд┐ рдЪ рджрдзреНрдпрд╛рджреЗрдГ рд╢реБрдХреНрддреАрднреВрддрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ ред рдпрджрд┐ рддреБ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рдореН рдЖрд╢реНрд░рд┐рддреНрдп рдкреБрдирдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдз рдЙрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЛ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдпрддреЗ, рддрдерд╛ рд╕рддрд┐ рди рдХрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рджреН рджреЛрд╖рдГ ред
  • рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдирд╛рдВ рдорд╢рдХрдордХреНрд╖рд┐рдХрд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рдмрд╛рд▓реНрдпрд╛рджреН рдзрд┐рдВрд╕рдиреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреЗ рдпрддреНрдирддрдГ рдкрд░рд┐рд╣рд╛рд░рд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдкреБрдирдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрдГ ред рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╡рд┐рдзреНрдпрдЩреНрдЧрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдереЛ рд╡рд╛ ред рди рдХреЗрд╡рд▓рдВ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдердкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдХреНрд░рдореЛ39 рдпрд╛рд╡рддреН рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╡рд┐рдзреНрдпрд░реНрдерд╛рддрд┐рдХреНрд░рдореЛ рд╜рдкрд┐ ред рд╢реБрдХреНрддрд╛рджрд┐рд╖реНрд╡реН рдЕрдкреНрдпреН рдПрд╡рдВ рдХрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рди рдХрд▓реНрдкреНрдпрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪреЗрджреН рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐ рддрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд░реЗ рд╕рд╛рд╡рдХрд╛рд╢рддреНрд╡рдореН, рдПрдХрд░реВрдкрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╡реНрдпрд░реНрдерддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕рддрд┐ рдЧрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░реЗ рдЧрд░реАрдпрдГ рее реи.резренрен рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШMadhuтАЩтАФstands for the honey produced by bees. As for wine (which also is called тАШmadhuтАЩ), it is an intoxicant; and hence its use is prohibited even before the Upanayana: тАШThe Br─Бhmaс╣Зa should ever abstain from intoxicantsтАЩтАФsays Gautama (2.20).

тАШMeat,тАЩтАФeven such as has been offered (to deities And fathers).

The term тАШscentтАЩ stands for camphor and such other things as are of extremely sweet scent,тАФthe name of the quality (scent) being used figuratively for things possessed of it. All highly perfumed substances are prohibited, and what is prohibited is the applying of these perfumes to the body; as for the scent itself, when it proceeds from the fragrant substance, it cannot, be checked. Nor does the prohibition apply to the case where the perfume reaches the student by chance. What is reprehensible therefore is the intentional using of fragrant incense and such things as luxury. It is for this reason that there.is nothing reprehensible in the case where the pupil is told by his Teacher to cut a Sandal-tree and the sweet smell of the wood reaches him it its natural way. It Is by reason of its being mentioned along with тАШgarlandтАЩ that we take it to mean strong scent. That which is not strong enough to exhilarate the mind,тАФe.g., the smell of such things as Kuс╣гс╣нha, Ghс╣Ыta, P┼лtid─Бru, etc.тАФis not prohibited.

тАШGarlandтАЩтАФflowers strung together.

тАШFlavoursтАЩтАФSweet, acid and the rest.

тАЬSince things absolutely devoid of flavour could not be eaten, living itself would be impossible (if one were to avoid all flavours).тАЭ

True; but what are prohibited are highly tasty things, like sugar. This prohibition applies also to such substances as are mixed with other things, by way of condiments. Or, the prohibition may apply to too much indulgence in too richly cooked and tasty food. To the same end we have the following sayingтАФтАШHe alone acquires learning who shuns wealth like serpent, sweets like poison and women like demonesses.тАЩ

Others explain тАШrasa,тАЩ тАШflavour,тАЩ to stand for the poetic emotions, Erotic and the rest; the sense being that one should not arouse his emotions by witnessing dramatic performances or listening to poetical recitations.

Others again have held the view that the prohibition applies to the pieces of sugar-cane, Dh─Бtri and such other substances, when extracted and separated from them,тАФand not as contained within them.

This however is not right; the term тАШrasaтАЩ is not known as symonymous with тАШfluid.тАЩ

As a matter of fact, what is prohibited with regard to each of the things named is its enjoyment, in whatever form this may be possible. For instance, of honey and meat, what is prohibited is the eating, and not the seeing or touching; of scent and garland, what is prohibited is using them with the idea of adorning the body, and not merely holding them by the hand; similarly in the case of women, it is sexual intercourse that is prohibited; and it is by reason of there being a fear of suchтАЩintercourse following that the author is going to prohibit later on, the looking at, and touching of, women. As says Gautama (2.16)тАФтАШThe looking at, and touching of women (are reprehensible), for fear of its leading to actual intercourse.тАЩ

тАШFermented acidsтАЩтАФsuch things as turn acid; that is those that turn acid either by being kept overnight, or by being mixed with other substances. Such substances are prohibited by reason of the avoiding of these being among the duties of all twice-born persons; and yet it has been re-iterated here for the purpose of including all those things that are named тАШacidтАЩ only figuratively; it is thus that тАШharsh wordsтАЩ become prohibited. Says GautamaтАФтАШAcid words (should be avoided).тАЩ It is for the purpose of including all this that the author has added the epithet тАШall.тАЩ This epithet тАШallтАЩ is meant to refer to тАШflavoursтАЩ and тАШacids.тАЩ It is thus that the figurative use becomes established.

Some people offer the following explanation:тАФтАЬThe term тАШacidтАЩ prohibits the acid flavours, and the term тАШallтАЩ prohibits unpleasant words.тАЭ

These people should be asked the following question:тАФWhy cannot the epithet тАШallтАЩ be taken as prohibiting those things that are prohibited only by implication r In this way we could obtain the prohibition of curds and like things which have turned acid. If however the prohibition (by тАШallтАЩ) be explained as referring to things whose use is possible,тАФthen there can be no objection to it.

тАШOf living creatures,тАЩтАФsuch as insects and fleas; the killing of these is done through childishness; hence we have the present prohibition with a view to emphasise the necessity of making special efforts to avoid it. Or, the re-iteration of the prohibition may be meant to be indicative of the fact that the avoidance of killing is auxiliary to тАШVedic Study.тАЩ So that the killing would involve the transgression, not only of the prohibition calculated for the benefit of the agent, but also that of the due observance of the injunction of Vedic Study.

тАЬWhy is not the same assumption made regarding the fermented acids and other things also?тАЭ

The prohibition of the acids, etc., is such as has room for it in other cases also [ e.g. Harsh words are prohibited for other people and under other circumstances also; the prohibition of killing has no such room for application, since it is necessary during sacrificial performances]. And when between two things it is found that one becomes absolutely null and void, while there is still room for the other, then preference is given to the former.тАФ(177)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШRas─БnтАЩтАФтАЬMolasses and the likeтАЩ (Govindar─Бja, Kull┼лka and N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa);тАФтАШclarified butter, oil and the likeтАЩ (Nandana);тАФтАШsweet, acid and the rest;тАФi.e. very richly flavoured foodтАЩ (Medh─Бtithi, who also notes oneтАШotherтАЩ explanation, juices of sugar-cane, tamarind and other fruits, which he rejects);тАФN─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa mentions one explanation, тАШpoetic sentimentsтАЩ.

This is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 456), along with the next two verses and a half, as enumerating the things to be avoided by the Student;тАФin V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 494), which adds the notes: тАШRas─БnтАЩ stands for the juices of sugar-cane and other things;тАФeven though Honey also is a juice, yet it has been mentioned separately in view of the heavier expiatory rites prescribed for the transgressors of the rule prohibiting it.

The verse is quoted also in Madanop─Бrj─Бta (p. 39) as enumerating the things prohibited for the Student;тАФand in Apar─Бrka (p. 62);тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 42);тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 125), which adds the following notes:тАФтАШRasaтАЩ stands for the sugar-cane juice and the rest; though тАШmadhuтАЩ also is a тАШrasa,тАЩ yet it is mentioned separately with a view to indicate that the taking of it involves a heavier expiation.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

**(verses 177-179)
**

Gautama (2.19).тАФтАШHe should abstain from honey, meat, scents, garland and the like, sleeping during the day, anointing, riding on conveyances, applying collyrium, wearing shoes, umbrella, attachment, anger, avarice, delusion, wrangling, bathing, teeth-cleansing, rejoicing, dancing, singing, calumniating and dangers.тАЩ

─Аpastamba-Dharmas┼лtra (1.23-26).тАФтАШAvoiding saline salts, honey and meat; not using scents;тАФhe should never have recourse to sexual intercourse;тАФfree from anger, and jealousy.тАЩ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШAnointingтАЩтАФrubbing of the head and body with butter, oil or such other oily substances.

тАШApplying collyrium to the eyesтАФthe addition of the word тАШeyesтАЩ is only for the purpose of filling up the metre.

What is prohibited in regard to these two is the having recourse to them by way of ornamentation; and not their use as medicine. That this is so is. dear from their being mentioned along with тАШscents and garlands.тАЩ

тАШShoesтАЩтАФfoot-covers made of leather; not all kinds of foot-cover.

тАШHolding of the umbrellaтАЩтАФeither by oneтАЩs own hand or by the hand of another person; both are prohibited.

тАШK─БmaтАЩ here stands for attachment; the preclusion of sexual desire being already included under the prohibition of association with women (in 177).

тАШAngerтАЩтАФrage.

тАШAvariceтАЩтАФselfishness. Notions of тАШIтАЩ and тАШmineтАЩ are the characteristics of the mind.

тАШDancing.тАЩтАФThe throwing about of oneтАЩs limbs for the delectation of ordinary people, as also the acting of dramas according to the rules laid down by Bharata and others.

тАШSingingтАЩтАФthe exhibition of the тАШс╣вaс╕НjaтАЩ and other musical notes.

тАШPlaying upon musical instruments,’тАФthe producing of musical sounds by means of the lute, the flute and so forth, as also the striking, to time, of such instruments as the drum, mс╣Ыdaс╣Еga and the like.тАФ(178)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШGambling;тАЩтАФplaying with dice. Cock-fighting, etc., are also prohibited by this,тАФthe term тАШgamblingтАЩ being used in its most general sense.

тАШQuarelling with peopleтАЩ;тАФwordy dispute, without any reason, on common matters; or asking people at random for news.

тАШCalumniating.тАЩтАФRecounting the defects of other people through sheer ill-will.

тАШLyingтАЩтАФdescribing things otherwise than what is actually seen or heard.

Every one of these words has the Accusative ending, on account of its being governed by the verb тАШshould abstain fromтАЩ (in the preceding verse).

тАШThe gazing at and touching of womenтАЩ;тАФтАШgazing atтАЩ means looking intently with a view to observe the shape of limbs; тАШthis part of her body is beautifulтАФthat is not so,тАЩand so forth.

тАШTouchingтАЩ stands for embracing. These two are prohibited for fear of their leading up to sexual intercourse; and this is to be applied to the case of the young boy in some way or other.

тАШInjuring of others,тАЩтАФi.e., doing harm; obstructing the fulfilment of some purpose. For instance, if he is questioned on matters relating to the marriage of girls, he should not say that a certain bridegroom is unfit, even if he be really so; he should remain quiet (say nothing), as lying has been prohibited.тАФ(179)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

When one renounces his vow of continence intentionally, then he has to perform the expiatory rite prescribed for the тАШAvak─лrс╣З─лтАЩ (11.120 et. seq.); the present verse lays down what one should do when he does it unintentionally.

No significance attaches to the mention of тАШdreamтАЩ; the absence of intention is the only necessary condition; and no intention can be present during dreams. Hence this same expiatory rite is to be performed in a case where, even though he may be not asleep, the flow occurs involuntarily, in the same manner as certain other fluids flow out of the body.

The sense of the verse thus is thatтАФтАШif one drops his manhood unintentionally, he should perform this expiatory rite that he should recite the three verses, etc., etc.тАФ(181)

рдкрд░реНрдпреБрд╖рд┐рддреЗрдирд╛рдкрд┐ рдШреГрддрд╛рджрд┐рд╕реНрдиреЗрд╣рд╕рдВрдпреБрдХреНрддреЗрди рд╕реНрдпрд╛рджреН рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рд╕реН рддрджрд░реНрдердореН рдЗрджрдореН- рдЕрд╣рд░реН рдЕрд╣рд░реН рднрд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рд╢рд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рди рдкреБрдирд░реН рдПрдХрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдиреН рдЕрд╣рдирд┐ рднрд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрдореН рдЕрдкрд░реЗрджреНрдпреБрдГ рдкрд░рд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕реНрдп рдпрддреН рдХрд┐рдВрдЪрд┐рддреН рд╕реНрдиреЗрд╣рдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╕рд╡реЗрди рднреБрдЮреНрдЬреАрдд рее реи.резреореи рее

рдпреЗрднреНрдпреЛ рднреИрдХреНрд╖рдореН рдЖрд╕рд╛рджрдпрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рддрд╛рдиреН рд╡рдХреНрддрд┐ ред

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

He should fetch as much of water in jars and other things as might serve the purposes of the Teacher.

This is only by way of illustration; the meaning being that he should do other household-work also,тАФall that is not absolutely demeaning. What this verse is meant to indicate is that the pupil should not be made to do any demeaning work,тАФsuch as touching the utensils in which food has been eaten by persons other than the Teacher himself. For as regards the Teacher himself, his service has been already prescribed in a general way.

The compound тАШy─Бvadarth─БniтАЩ is to be expounded as тАШy─Бv─Бn arthaс╕е eс╣г─Бm.тАЩ

тАШDay by day he should beg for almsтАЩ;тАФтАШalmsтАЩ here stands for a very small quantity of cooked, just enough for sustenance. It would not be right to argue that it stands for food in general (not necessarily cooked); since the generic term тАШannaтАЩ (food) is found to be used in the prohibition coming later on (in 188) regarding тАШthe food of one personтАЩ; because in view of the injunction тАШhaving collected the alms, he should present it to the Teacher and then eat it,тАЩ where the bringing and eating are mentioned together, it is clear that cooked food is meant; if dry grains had been brought in, how could they be eaten forthwith? If the grain were collected and then cooked in the TeacherтАЩs house, the food thus cooked would be one that has the alms for its source, it would not be the aims itself. In common usage also it is cooked food that is called тАШalms.тАЩ

тАШDay by day.тАЩтАФтАЬThe daily begging for alms is already implied in what follows later on (in 188)тАФтАШHe should live every day on alms.тАЩ

In 188, the term тАШevery dayтАЩ has been added for the purpose of laying down the means of subsistence; while the term тАШday by dayтАЩ in the present verse is meant to preclude the possibility of some one keeping the food mixed with butter, etc., overnight and then eating it next day; the sense being that he should beg for alms and eat it day by day; and he should never beg on one day and then, having kept it over-night, eat it next day after mixing it with butter, etcтАФ(182)

The Author next mentions the persons from whom the alms are to be begged.

тАШWho are not devoid of Veda and sacrificesтАФwho are equipped with Vedic learning, and perform the sacrifices to which they are entitled;тАФтАШnot devoidтАЩ means not without, i.e., fully equipped.

Even though the TeacherтАЩs family may fulfil the aforesaid conditions, yet тАШhe should not beg for foodтАЩ from that family. тАШKula,тАЩ тАШfamily,тАЩ stands for тАШrelationsтАЩ; hence one should not receive alms from the uncle and other relations of the Teacher.

тАШPaternal relationsтАЩтАФfrom the family of those related to the student on his fatherтАЩs side.тАФтАШFrom his maternal relationsтАЩтАФi.e., from his maternal uncle and others.

тАЬFrom whom then is he to beg for food?тАЭ

From houses other than those here mentioned.

тАШWhen other houses are not availableтАЩтАФi.e., not possible;тАФwhen, for instance, the entire village is inhabited either by the TeacherтАЩs family, or by his own paternal and maternal relations; and there are no other families;тАФor even though they are there, they do not give him alms;тАФthen the student may beg from those just mentioned; when, others are uot available, he should first beg from his maternal relations; if these latter be not available, then from his paternal relations; and when even these arc not available, then from the TeacherтАЩs family.тАФ(184)

рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрдХреНрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡реЗрджрдпрдЬреНрдЮреИрд░реН рдЕрд╣реАрдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЕрд╕рдВрднрд╡реЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рдордореН рдЕрдирдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рд╡рд░реНрдгрд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧрдВ рд╡рд┐рдЪрд░реЗрддреН рднреНрд░рд╛рдореНрдпреЗрдЬреН рдЬреАрд╡рдирд░реНрдердореН ред рдХреЗрд╡рд▓рдореН рдЕрднрд┐рд╢рд╕реНрддрд╛рдиреН рдХреГрддрдкрд╛рддрдХрддреНрд╡реЗрди рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛рдиреН рдЕрджреГрд╖реНрдЯрдкрд╛рддрдХрд╛рдиреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рд╡рд░реНрдЬрдпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рдЧреМрддрдордГ- “рд╕рд╛рд░реНрд╡рд╡рд░реНрдгрд┐рдХрдВ рднреИрдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдЪрд░рдгрдореН рдЕрднрд┐рд╢рд╕реНрддрдкрддрд┐рддрд╡рд░реНрдЬрдореН” (рдЧреНрдзреН реи.рейрел) ред рдирд┐рдпрдореНрдп рд╡рд╛рдЪрдВ рднрд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд░реНрдЬрдпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЖ рднреИрдХреНрд╖рд▓рд╛рднрд╛рджреН рдЕрдиреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдВ рдиреЛрдЪреНрдЪрд░реЗрддреН рее реи.резреорел рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШAll the aforesaidтАЩтАФi.e., those not devoid of the Veda and sacrifices and so forthтАФтАШbeing unavailableтАЩ;тАФтАШwander over the whole villageтАЩ;тАФhe may go over the whole village, irrespectively of caste and other distinctions, for the purpose of obtaining his means of subsistence. Only тАШhe should avoid persons of ill-reputeтАЩтАФi.e., those who are known to have committed serious sins, even though they may never have been seen to commit them; Says Gautama (2-35)тАФтАШThe begging of alms may be done from all castes, save the disreputable and the fallen.тАЩ

тАШHaving his speech well-controlledтАЩ;тАФi.e., till he obtains the alms, he should not utter any words save those used in the actual begging.тАФ(186)

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рджреВрд░рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдореН рдЕрдкрд░рд┐рдЧреГрд╣реАрддрджреЗрд╢реЛрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рд░реНрдердореН ред рдЧреНрд░рд╛рдорд╛рддреН рдХрд┐рд▓ рджреВрд░рдореН рдЕрд░рдгреНрдпрдореН, рди рдЪ рддрддреНрд░ рдХрд╕реНрдпрдЪрд┐рддреН рдкрд░рд┐рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдГ ред рдЕрдиреБрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгреЗ рд╣рд┐ рджреВрд░рд╛рд░реНрдереЗ рдХрд┐рдпрджреН рджреВрд░рдореН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрдирд╡рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрдГ рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдердГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рдЖрд╣реГрддреНрдп рдЖрдиреАрдп ред рд╕рдВрдирд┐рджрдзреНрдпрд╛рддреН рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрдпреЗрддреН ред рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рдпрд╕рд┐ рдЧреГрд╣рд╕реНрдпреЛрдкрд░рд┐ ред рди рд╣рд┐ рдирд┐рд░рд╛рд▓рдореНрдмрдиреЗ рд╜рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рдирд┐рдзрд╛рдирдВ рд╕рдВрднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рддрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╛рдпрдВрдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд░реН рдЬреБрд╣реБрдпрд╛рддреН ред рдЖрд╣рд░рдгрдВ рддреБ рддрд╛рддреНрдХрд╛рд▓рд┐рдХрдореН рдЕрдиреНрдпрджрд╛ рд╡реЗрдЪреНрдЫрдпрд╛ ред рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рдпрд╕рд┐51 рдирд┐рдзрд╛рдирдореН рдЕрджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд░реНрдердореН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЖрд╣реБрдГ ред рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗ рддреБ рдмреНрд░реБрд╡рддреЗ рд╕рдВрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд╛рдиреАрдпреНрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖рд╛рджреН рджрд╛рд░реБ рдЖрд░реНрджреНрд░рдВ рднрд╡рддреАрддрд┐, рдЧреГрд╣рд╕реНрдпреЛрдкрд░рд┐ рдЕрдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рджреЗрд╕реН рддрдд рдПрд╡рд╛рд╡рдЧрдиреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН рее реи.резреорем рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The term тАШdistanceтАЩ is meant to stand for such plots of land as are not owned by any one; for instance, the forest is тАШdistantтАЩ from the village, and it is not owned by any one. If such were not the meaning, and тАШdistanceтАЩ simply meant тАШremote places,тАЩтАФthen since the exact degree of remoteness is not specified, the manning of the injunction would remain indefinite.

тАШHaving fetchedтАЩтАФhaving brought.

тАШShould placeтАЩтАФshould keep.

тАШIn the airтАЩтАФi.e., on the roof of the house; no placing is possible in the open air, without some support.

тАШWith these he should make offerings morning and evening.тАЩ

The fetching of the fuel may he at that or at any other time, according as the student pleases.

Some people regard the тАШplacing in the airтАЩ as serving some transcendental purpose. Others have however held that the fuel brought fresh from the tree is wet; and hence it is necessary to place it either on the top of the house or on that of a wall, etc. (for the purpose of drying).тАФ(186)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШVih─БyasiтАЩтАФIn the air, i. e. on the roof of the house (Medh─Бtithi, Govindar─Бja and Kull┼лka);тАФтАШon a platformтАЩ (N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa);тАФтАШin the open air (Nandana);тАФтАШin any pure place except the groundтАЩ (R─Бghav─Бnanda).

This verse is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 451), as laying down the method of тАШtending the fireтАЩ, and тАШexplains it that тАШhe should place the fuel somewhere in the open, not on the grouhd;тАЩтАФin Smс╣Ыtitattva (p. 936) as laying down the morning and evening offerings into the Fire;тАФin V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 448), where тАШd┼лr─БtтАЩ is explained as from a spot not owned by any oneтАЩ;тАФin Vidh─Бnap─Бrij─Бta (p. 498), where vih─Бyasi is explained as тАШantar─лkс╣гeтАЩ тАШin the open airтАФin Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 24), where тАШd┼лr─БtтАЩ is explained as тАШfrom a spot not owned by any other personтАЩ, and тАШvih─БyasiтАЩ as тАШmaс╣Зс╕Нap─БdauтАЩ тАШoh an altar or some such placeтАЩ;тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 43), which says that, according to Dharmaprak─Б┼Ыa, тАШvih─БyasiтАЩ means тАШon the house-topтАЩ;тАФin Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 86), which explains d┼лr─Бt, as тАШfrom places not belonging to any personтАЩ, and vih─Бyasi as тАШon the house-topтАЩ,тАФand in Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 34a).

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

  • рдпреЗ рддреБ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЪрдХреНрд╖рддреЗ рд╕рдкреНрддрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рдореН рдПрддрджреН рдЙрднрдпрдореН рдЕрд╡рд╢реНрдпрдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рдЕрдХрд░рдгрд╛рддреН рддрддреНрд░ рджреЛрд╖рдГ ред рдХреГрддрд╕рдкреНрддрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рддреБ рдкрд░рддреЛ рд╜рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рди рджреЛрд╖рдГ ред рддрд╛рдирд┐ рдЪ рд╕рдкреНрддрд╛рд╣рд╛рдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдердореНрдпрд╛рджреН рдЙрдкрдирдпрдирд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рднреГрддрд┐ рдЧреГрд╣реНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рддрджреН рдПрддрджреН рдЕрдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН “рдЖ рд╕рдорд╛рд╡рд░реНрддрдирд╛рддреН рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН” (рдореНрдзреН реи.резрежрео) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд░реЛрдзрд╛рддреН ред рдЙрдкрд░рд┐рддрдирд╛рдирдиреНрддрд░рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХрд╡рд┐рд░реЛрдзрд╛рдЪреН рдЪ рее реи.резреорен рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШHe who, for seven daysтАЩтАФconsecutively, тАШhas omitted to beg alms and to offer fuel to the Fire,тАФwithout being illтАЩтАФwhile not suffering from any disease,тАФтАШshall perform the rites prescribed for the Anak─лrс╣ЗinтАЩ;тАФi.e., the expiatory rite the exact form of which is going to he described in Chap. 11?. (verse 118).

This is said here only for the purpose of showing the gravity of the offence; and it does not mean that the rite mentioned is to he actually performed in expiation of the omission. That this is so is shown by the fact that another Smс╣Ыti has laid down a much simpler expiation for this omission, viz.: тАШoffering of clarified butter, etc.тАЩ The following fact also is another indicative of the same conclusion:тАФIf what is mentioned here were a real expiatory rite, then on the occasion of mentioning the conditions under which the тАШAmk─лrс╣Зin-riteтАЩ are to be performed as an expiatory rite, the author would have mentioned these omissions also, in the same way in which he has mentioned тАШsexual intercourse with women.тАЩ

Some people interpret this verse to means as follows:тАФтАЬIt is necessary to do the two acts (of begging alms and offering fuel) for seven days only; having done them for seven days, if one drops them, there is no harm in this; and these seven days are to be the first ones after Upanayana.тАЭ

This however is not right; as it would lie in direct contravention to the direction that тАШthis should be done till the Final Return from the teacherтАЩs house,тАЩтАФas also to what follows in the next verse.тАФ(187)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (Pr─Бya┼Ыcitta, p. 438) as laying down the Avak─лrс╣Зivrata (actually prescribed in 11.118 in connection with the loss of chastity on the part of the Student) as applicable to other omissions also;тАФin V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra p. 485), in support of the view that the Begging of Alms is not optional, but compulsory, since the present verse prescribes an expiation for its omission, which clearly implies that the omission is sinful;тАФin Vidh─Бnap─Бrij─Бta (p. 498) to the effect that the omission of Begging alms involves sin; and again on page 500, where it is explained that the expiation here prescribed is to be performed in the event of repeated omissions;тАФand in Mit─Бkс╣гar─Б (p. 1345, on 3. 281), where it is explained as laying down an expiation for those cases where the duty of тАШfire-tendingтАЩ is omitted without any such extenuating circumstance as being occupied with some other duty.

Nirс╣Зayosindhu (p. 190) quotes it as laying down the expiatory rites due on the omission of the duties laid down for the Student.

It is quoted in Apar─Бrka (p. 1142) as laying down the expiation for omitting the said duties, without sufficient reason;тАФin Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 111) to the effect that alms-begging is an obligatory duty;тАФand in Saс╣Гsk─Бraratnam─Бl─Б (p. 357).

Viс╣гс╣Зu (28.52)тАФ(reproduces ManuтАЩs words).

  • рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдерд╡рд╛рджрдГ57 ред рднреИрдХреНрд╖реЗрдгреИрд╡ рдХреЗрд╡рд▓реЗрди рд╡реНрд░рддрд┐рдиреЛ рдпрд╛ рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рдГ рд╢рд░реАрд░рдзрд╛рд░рдгрдореН рдЙрдкрд╡рд╛рд╕рддреБрд▓реНрдпрдлрд▓рд╛ рд╕рд╛ рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрдорд░реНрдпрддреЗ рее реи.резреорео рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

Objection.тАФтАЬIt has already been laid down that he should go about begging alms every day (183).тАЭ

What is there said would show that the begging of Alms is meant to serve the visible purpose (of sustaining the body); specially as it has been subsequently laid down that тАШhaving offered it to the Teacher, he should eat itтАЩ; and this тАШeatingтАЩ cannot be sanctificatory of the alms; which alone could prevent us from taking it as serving the purely visible purpose of sustaining the body.

Some people have explained that the re-iteration of the тАШdaily begging of almsтАЩ is made for the purpose of adding the further direction that тАШhe should not eat the food given by one person.тАЩ

But this is not right. Since the eating of the food given by one person is precluded by the term тАШalmsтАЩ itself. тАШAlmsтАЩ stands for an aggregate of what is obtained by begging; whence then could there be any possibility of eating the food given by one person?

The conclusion on this point is that the whole rule has been re-iterated here with a view to adding (in the next verse) that such eating of the food given by one person is permissible at ┼Ъr─Бddhas.

тАШHe should subsist on almsтАЩ;тАФhe should nourish his bodyтАФsustain his lifeтАФby means of food obtained by begging; and he should not eat food received from a single person.

The verse should not be taken to mean that тАЬhe should not eat what belongs to a single person,тАФhe should eat what belongs to several owners; e.g., what belongs to several undivided brothers.тАЭ For the word in the text means simply тАШone who eats one foodтАФor one personтАЩs food.тАЩ

The term тАШVratiтАЩ here stands for the Religious Student; and as the fact of the rule pertaining to him is clear from the context, the addition of the word can be taken only as filing up the metre.

Next follows the commendatory statement:тАФтАШThe subsistingтАФsustaining of the bodyтАФof the student on alms only has been declared to be equal to fasting.тАЩтАФ(188)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

The first half of the verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 454) in support of the view that the Student should not accept food from one and the same house day after day; and adds that this is meant to apply to normal times; in abnormal times it is not meant to be strictly adhered to; this on the strength of Y─Бj├▒avalkyaтАЩs declaration (1. 32.)

The same work quotes the second half of the verse on p. 485, as declaring the reward accruing to the Student from strictly following the rules of alms-begging.

The whole verse is quoted in Vidh─Бnap─Бrij─Бta (p. 498) as prohibiting the habit of seeking for food from one and the same person regularly;тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 61);тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 111), which says that this refers to normal times, not to abnormal times of distress.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

**(verses 2.188-189)
**

188 He who performs the vow (of studentship) shall constantly subsist on alms, (but) not eat the food of one (person only); the subsistence of a student on begged food is declared to be equal (in merit) to fasting.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдореВрд▓рд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

During a performance in honour of gods and in honour of ancestors, he may, when invited, eat freely, like an ascetic, in due accordance with his observances. by this his observances do not suffer.тАФ(189)

рдЕрдпрдореН рдЕрдкрд╡рд╛рджреЛ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЗ рднреИрдХреНрд╖рд╡реГрддреНрддреНрдпреБрдкрджреЗрд╢рд╕реНрдп ред рджреЗрд╡рджреИрд╡рддреНрдпреЗ рджреЗрд╡реЛрджреНрджреЗрд╢реЗрди рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрднреЛрдЬрдиреЗ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрдорд╛рдгреЗ, рдкрд┐рддреНрд░реНрдпреЗ рдЪ рдкрд┐рддреДрдиреН рдЙрджреНрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрд╛рднреНрдпрд░реНрдерд┐рддреЛ рд╜рдзреНрдпреЗрд╖рд┐рддрдГ, рдХрд╛рдордореН рдПрдХрд╛рдиреНрдирдореН рдЕрд╢реНрдиреАрдпрд╛рддреН ред рди рддреБ рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдВ рдпрд╛рдЪреЗрдд ред рддрдЪреН рдЪ58 рд╡реНрд░рддрд╡рджреН рд╡реНрд░рддрд╛рд╡рд┐рд░реБрджреНрдзрдВ59 рдордзреБрдорд╛рдВрд╕рд╡рд░реНрдЬрд┐рддрдореН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрд░реНрдердГ ред рд╡реНрд░рддрд╡рджреН рдЛрд╖рд┐рд╡рджреН рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪ рд╢рдмреНрджрджреНрд╡рдпреЗрдиреИрдХ рдПрд╡рд╛рд░реНрде рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ, рди рдкреБрдирд░реН рдЧреНрд░рд╛рдорд╛рд░рдгреНрдпрдпреЛрдГ рдХрд░реНрдорднреЗрджреЗрди рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛ ред рд╡реГрддреНрддрд╛рдиреБрд░реЛрдзрд╛рддреН рддреБ рджреНрд╡рд┐рд░рднрд┐рдзрд╛рдирдореН ред рдЛрд╖рд┐рд░реН рд╡реИрдЦрд╛рдирд╕рд╕реН рддрджрд╢рдирд╛рднреНрдпрдиреБрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдиреЗ рдорд╛рдВрд╕рдореН рдЕрдкрд┐ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд╛рд░рд┐рдгреЛ рд╜рдиреБрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддрдВ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рддрд╕реНрдп рд╣рд┐ “рд╡реИрд╖реНрдХрдореН рдЕрдкреНрдпреН рдЙрдкрднреБрдЮреНрдЬреАрдд” (рдЧреНрдзреН рей.рейрез) рдЗрддрд┐ рдорд╛рдВрд╕рд╛рд╢рдирдореН рдЕрдкреНрдпреН рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐ ред рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ рдпрд╕реНрдп рддрджреН рджреЗрд╡рджреИрд╡рддреНрдпрдореН ред рддрдЪреН рдЪрд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╣реЛрддреНрд░рджрд░реНрд╢рдкреВрд░реНрдгрдорд╛рд╕рд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ рджреИрд╡реЗрд╖реБ рдХрд░реНрдорд╕реБ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрднреЛрдЬрдирдореН рдЖрдореНрдирд╛рддрдореН, рдЖрдЧреНрд░рд╣рд╛рдпрдгреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ рдЪрд╛рдореНрдирд╛рддрдореН60 “рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рдиреН рднреЛрдЬрдпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддреНрдпрдпрдирдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдпреЗрддреН” рдЗрддрд┐ ред рддрддреНрд░реЗрдпрдореН рдЕрдиреБрдЬреНрдЮрд╛ ред

  • рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗ рддреБ рд╕рдкреНрддрдореНрдпрд╛рджрд╛рд╡реН рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рджреЗрд╡реЛрджреНрджреЗрд╢реЗрди рдпрддреН рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрднреЛрдЬрдирдВ рддрджреН рджреЗрд╡рджреИрд╡рддреНрдпрдВ рдордиреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рддрджреН рдЕрд╕рддреН ред рди рд╣рд┐ рднреБрдЬреЗрд░реН рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзреЛ рд╜рд╕реНрддрд┐, рдЕрдпрд╛рдЧрд╕рд╛рдзрдирддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рддрд╕реНрдп ред рди рддреВрджреНрджреЗрд╢реНрдпрдорд╛рддреНрд░рдВ61 рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛, “рдЙрдкрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдп рдЧрд╛рдВ рджрджрд╛рддрд┐,” “рдЧреГрд╣рдВ рд╕рдВрдорд╛рд░реНрд╖реНрдЯрд┐” рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЙрдкрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рдЧреГрд╣реЗ рд╜рдкрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрд╛рддреН ред рднреБрдЬреЗрд░реН рд╣рд┐ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖реЛ рднреЛрдХреНрддреНрд░рд╛ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ ред рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╕реН рддреБ рди рдХрд╛рд░рдХрдореН, рди рдЪреЛрджреНрджреЗрд╢реНрдпреЛ рдЧреГрд╣рд╡рддреН, рди рддрджрд░реНрдердВ рднреЛрдЬрдирдореН ред рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛ рд╣рд┐ рднреЛрдХреНрддреНрд░рд░реНрдерддрд╛рдВ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкрдпрддрд┐, рдирд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерддрд╛рдореН ред рди рдЪреИрддрддреН рдХреНрд╡рдЪрд┐рдиреН рдиреЛрджрд┐рддрдореН “рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпреБрджреНрджреЗрд╢реЗрди рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рдиреН рднреЛрдЬрдпреЗрддреН” рдЗрддрд┐ ред

  • рдПрд╡рдВ “рджреИрд╡рддрд╛рдиреНрдпреН рдЕрднрд┐рдЧрдЪреНрдЫреЗрддреН” рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдкрд╛рджрд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрд╛рд░реЗрдг рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рд╕рдореАрдкрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреНрдпрд╕рдВрднрд╡рд╛рджреН рдЧрдореЗрд╢реН рдЪ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рд░реНрдерддреНрд╡рд╛рджреН рдЕрднрд┐рдЧрдордирдВ рд╕реНрдорд░рдгрд╛рддреН рдХрд┐рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдпрддреЗ ред рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ рдЕрднрд┐рдЧрдЪреНрдЫреЗрддреН, рдХрд░реНрдордХрд╛рд▓реЗ рдордирд╕рд╛ рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗрдЪреН рдЪрд┐рддреНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдХреНрд╖реЗрдкрддрд╛рдореН рдЖрдХреБрд▓рддрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдкрд░рд┐рд╣рд░реЗрджреН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрд░реНрдердГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪреЛрдкрд▓рднреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдореВрд▓реИрд╡реЗрдпрдВ рд╕реНрдореГрддрд┐рд░реН рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рдпрд╕реНрдпреИ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдпреИ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реН рдЧреГрд╣реАрддрдВ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН рддрд╛рдВ рдордирд╕рд╛ рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗрджреН рдЗрддрд┐ ред

  • рдирдиреБ рдЪреИрддрджреН рдЕрдкреНрдпреН рдЙрджреНрджреЗрд╢реНрдпрддреНрд╡рд╛рдиреНрдпрдерд╛рдиреБрдкрдкрддреНрддреЗрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдореН рдПрд╡ ред рд╕рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдХреНрд╖реЗрдкрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдХреБрд▓рд╕реНрдп рдЪ рд╕рдВрднрд╡рд╛рджреН рдЕрджреЛрд╖рдГ ред рдПрд╡рдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╕реНрд╡рдВ рджреЗрд╡рдкрд╢рд╡реЛ рджреЗрд╡рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрдореН рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрдпреЛ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рд╛рд╕реН рддрд╛рджрд░реНрдереНрдпреЗрдиреЛрдкрдХрд▓реНрдкрд┐рддреЗрд╖реБ рдкрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ рджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ ред

  • рджрдгреНрдбрд╛рдзрд┐рдХрд╛рд░реЗ рддреБ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдХреГрддрд┐рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдореН рдПрд╡ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рдореН рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЕрдиреНрдпрдерд╛ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рднрдЩреНрдЧрдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рдХрд▓реНрдкрд┐рддрджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рд░реВрдкрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдХреГрддреАрдирд╛рдВ рдХрд▓реНрдкрд┐рддреЗрдиреИрд╡ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рднрд╛рд╡реЗрди рдпрддреН рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рддрджреН рдПрд╡ “рджреЗрд╡рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдВ рддреБ рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮреЗрдпрдореН рдЙрддреНрддрдордореН” (рдиреНрд╕реНрдореН резрек.резрел) рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ рджреЗрд╡рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рди рд╣рд┐ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рднрд╛рд╡реЛ рд╜рд╕реНрддрд┐, рдореБрдЦреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рд╕рдВрднрд╡рд╛рджреН рдЧреМрдг рдПрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдереЛ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдпрдГ ред

  • рдХрдГ рдкреБрдирд░реН рдЕрддреНрд░ рдЧреМрдгреЛ рд╜рд░реНрдердГ ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рд╣рд┐ рд╕рд╛рдзрд╛рд░рдгрдЧреБрдгрдпреЛрдЧрд╛рджреН рдЧреМрдгрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рд╡рдЧрддрд┐рдГ85 ред рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реН86 рдорд╛рдгрд╡рдХ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ рд╢реБрдХреНрд▓реЗ87 рдорд╛рдгрд╡рдХреЗ рддрджреНрдЧреБрдгрджрд░реНрд╢рдирд╛рддреН ред рддреЗ рдЪ рдЧреБрдгрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд╛рджреНрдпрд╡рд╕реЗрдпрд╛рдГ88 ред рдЗрд╣ рддреБ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╛рд╡рдЧрдореНрдпрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрддрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╛рдирд╡рдЧрдорд╛рддреН рдХреБрддрдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдХреГрддрд┐рд╖реБ рд╕рд╛рдзрд╛рд░рдгрдЧреБрдгрд╛рд╡рд╕рд╛рдпрдГ ред

  • рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдерд╡рд╛рджреЗрд╖реБ рддрдерд╛рд╡рд┐рдзрд░реВрдкрд╢реНрд░рд╡рдгрд╛рддреН рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдЪ рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд╛рджреЗрди рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдирдореН ред рддрдиреНрдореВрд▓рдореН рдЕрдкрд╢реНрдпрдиреНрддреЛ рдпрдерд╛рд╢реНрд░реБрддрд╛рд░реНрдердЧреНрд░рд╛рд╣рд┐рдгрд╕реН рддрд╛рджреНрд░реВрдкреНрдпрдореН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ89 рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдХреГрддрд┐рд╖реБ рд╕рд╛рджреГрд╢реНрдпрдВ рдкрд╢реНрдпрдиреНрддреАрддрд┐90 рдпреБрдХреНрддреИрд╡ рдЧреМрдгрддрд╛ ред
  • рдпрддреН рддреБ рд╢реНрд░рд╛рджреНрдз рдПрд╡ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрднреЛрдЬрдирдВ рджреИрд╡рджреЗрд╡рддреНрдпрдореН рдЖрдЪрдХреНрд╖рддреЗ, рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдкрд┐рддреНрд░реНрдпрд╛рдЩреНрдЧрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рддрд╕реНрдп рдкрд┐рддреНрд░реНрдпрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгреЗрди рдЧреГрд╣реАрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рджреН рдЕрдирд░реНрдердХрдВ рдкреБрдирд░реНрд╡рдЪрдирдореН ред рд╕рд╛рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрд╢рдмреНрджрддреНрд╡рд╛рдЪреН рдЪ рдХреБрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╛рд╡рдЧрддрд┐рдГ ред рд╕рд╛рд╣рдЪрд░реНрдпрд╛рджреН рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪреЗрддреН, 91 рдпрджрд┐ рди92 рдкрд┐рддреНрд░реНрдпрд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдВ рднрд╡реЗрддреН ред рдЧреЛрдмрд▓реАрд╡рд░реНрджрдиреНрдпрд╛рдпреЛ рд╜рдкрд┐ рдЕрд╕рддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрднреЗрджреЗ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рее реи.резреореп рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

This verse provides an exception, under certain conditions, to the rules regarding subsisting on alms.

тАШIn honour of GodsтАЩ;тАФi.e., when Br─Бhmaс╣Зas are fed in honour of the gods; and also when they are fed in honour of the fathers;тАФif he is тАШincited,тАЩ requestedтАФтАШhe may eat freelyтАЩтАФthe food given by one person. But he himself should not ask for it.

This again should be тАШin due accordance with his observancesтАЩ; i.e., he should avoid honey and meat, which are inconsistent with his observances. The two phrasesтАФтАШin due accordance with his observancesтАЩ and тАШlike an asceticтАЩтАФexpress the same meaning; and it does not mean that in a village he is to eat тАШin accordance with his observances,тАЩ while in the forest he is to eat тАШlike an ascetic.тАЩ It is with a view to filling up the metre that the two phrases have been used. [There is another reason why the phrase тАШlike an asceticтАЩ should not he taken separately]тАФтАШAsceticтАЩ here stands for the hermit, so if the student were permitted to eat тАШlike the hermit,тАЩ the eating of meat also would become allowed for him; as the hermit is permitted to eat meat, by such rules as тАШhe may eat the flesh of dead animalsтАЩ (Gautama, 3.31).

тАШIn honour of GodsтАЩ;тАФi.e., those rites of which gods are the deities; i.e., the feeding of Br─Бhmaс╣Зas laid down as to be done at the performance of the Agnihotra, the Dar┼Ыa-P┼лrс╣Зam─Бsa and the other sacrifices offered to the gods; as we find in such injunctions as тАШat the ─Аgrah─Бyaс╣Зa and other sacrifices one should feed Br─Бhmaс╣Зas and make them pronounce тАЬsvasti.тАЭтАЩ It is in connection with these that we have the present permission for the religious student.

Others explain the term тАШperformance in honour of the godsтАЩ to mean that feeding of Br─Бhmaс╣Зas which is done in honour of the Sun-god on the seventh day of the month, and so forth.

This however is not right. For the act of eating has no connection with the gods,тАФbeing, as it is, not instrumental in the accomplishment of any sacrifice. Further, the mere fact of an act being done with reference to a god, does not make the latter the тАШdeityтАЩ of that act; if it did, then the Teacher would have to be regarded as the тАШdeityтАЩ when one gives a cow to him, and the room will have to be regarded as the тАШdeityтАЩ when one sweeps it. Then again, it is with the eater that the act of eating is directly connected; and the Sun-god has no active function in the fulfilment of that act (as the Teacher is in the former case); nor is he the thing aimed at (as the room is in the latter case); as the eating is not for his sake. Further, the accusative ending (in the term denoting food) denotes that it is meant for the eater, not that it is meant for the Sun-god. Nor has it been enjoined anywhere that тАШone should feed Br─Бhmaс╣Зas for the sake of (with reference to) the Sun-god.тАЩ

It might be argued that on the basis of usage we assume the existence of such an injunction.

But this cannot be; because there is always some scriptural basis found for such assumption of injunctions.

тАЬIn the present case also we have such basis in the shape of the тАШexternalтАЩ Smс╣Ыtis.тАЭ

If there were such a Smс╣Ыti-rule, its meaning would be that тАШone should please the gods by feeding Br─Бhmaс╣Зas.тАЩ And it would not be right to assume such a meaning; as scriptural injunctions are aimed, not at pleasin the Gods, but at accomplishing what is prescribed by the injunctions. Then again, if such were the meaning of the Injunction, its connection with the Sun-god and others intended to be deities could not be based either upon an object, or upon a desired result; nor again could they be the purpose, as in the case of the act of piercing; nor are they desired for their own sake, like cattle and other desirable things, for the simple reason that they are not something to be enjoyed. If it were the satisfaction of the Sun-god that were desired,тАФthat also, will need a proof for its own existence; and there is no such proof available. Such a thing as the тАШsatisfaction of the Sun-godтАЩ is not known by Perception or other means of knowledge,тАФin the way that cattle, etc., are,тАФwhereby it could be desired and connected with the performance of sacrifices.

If the motive of the man be held to be the idea that тАЬthe Sun-god is my lord and he will endow me with a fruit desired by meтАЭ;тАФthis also cannot be accepted, as there is no proof for this either. There is no Injunction in support of this idea. It is only an Injunction that prompts to activity the person who is related to a certain well-known result, which also serves to single out the man so prompted; but it does not point to the presence of the result. What the Injunction points to is the fact that a certain act known by other means of knowledge as leading to a particular desirable result is related to the performance as his qualifying factor.

If it be held that the offering is a kind of тАШsacrifice,тАЩ and the feeding is a kind of disposal of it,тАФour answer is that that may be so regarded, if such is the usage of cultured people. But the feeding cannot be shown to have any direct connection with the deity; and as for connection through the intervening agency of the sacrife, that we do not object to. Then again, as a matter of fact, when people undertake the performance of such acts, they have no idea that they are performing a sacrifice; the only idea that they have is that when the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas have been fed, the particular deity would be satisfied. From all this it is clear that the Deity has no sort of action conducive to the act of feeding, nor is it the qualifying factor of any other thing that has such action. Thus then, the Deity is neither the object of the act, nor has it any connection with it. Nor again is it possible for the Sun-god and the rest to be regarded ns aimed at by the act; for in the act of feeding, it is the person fed that is aimed at; and it is the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas that are fed. Further, the mere fact of being aimed at does not make one the тАШdeityтАЩ; for in that case, when one gives a cow to the Teacher, or sweeps the room, the Teacher and the room would have to be regarded as тАШdeities.тАЩ

тАЬHow then is there to be Br─Бhmaс╣Зa-feeding at a performance in honour of ancestors? There also the fathers could not be the тАШdeitiesтАЩ of the act. The offerings made into the Fire could not be regarded as made in honour of the ancestor; as other deities are found to be mentioned in connection with them. And just as the тАШsatisfaction of the Sun-god,тАЩ so the тАШsatisfaction of ancestors also, cannot be regarded as the result to be accomplished, by the act; for the very same reason that the connection of such satisfaction with the Injunction is not cognisable by any other means of knowledge.тАЭ

To this some people make the following answer:тАФThe тАШsatisfaction of AncestorsтАЩ is clearly recognised (as the result to be accomplished). That such beings as the тАШFathersтАЩ do exist is proved by the fact of souls being imperishable; and it is only through their deeds that they become connected with physical bodies. The feeding of these тАШAncestorsтАЩ is the principal business, of which the reward has been described in the passageтАФтАШfeeding them, one obtains ample reward.тАЩ This reward could only consist in the satisfaction of the Ancestors; this тАШsatisfactionтАЩ again could only be in the form of happiness, mental contentment; it could not be in the form of physical gratification which follows, in the case of men, from the act of eating. This pleasure may sometimes accrue to the fathers during the different conditions of life in which they happen to be born under the influence of their own past deeds. The verbal root тАШtс╣ЫpтАЩ denotes only satisfaction; physical gratification is something different, and can be known only by other means of knowledge.

Against this the following objection might be raised:тАФтАЬIn as much as the Son is the nominative agent in the act of feeding, how could the result, which should accrue to the agent, accrue to the Ancestors,тАФas people versed in law do not regard actions as bringing rewards to persons other than the actual doers.тАЭ

Such an objection cannot be rightly taken. Because in this case the Ancestors themselves are the accredited agents; by the mere act of begetting the child, the father has done all this (that the son does on his behalf); in fact the son is begot for the sole purpose that he will confer on the Father benefits, seen as well as unseen. Tims then, just as in the Sarvasv─Бra sacrificeтАФwhere the performer offers his own life and is thus absent when the subsequent details are performed,тАФsome other persons continue to be regarded as the тАШperformer,тАЩ by virtue of his having died after having requested the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas to finish the sacrifice for him, by means of the words

тАШO Br─Бhmaс╣Зas, please finish the sacrifice for meтАЩ;тАФso would it also be in the case in question. The only difference between the two cases is tbat in the case of the Sarvasv─Бra, the actual doers are the hired priests doing the act with the totally different motive of earning a living, while in the case in question the doer is the son, who has been prompted by tbat same Injunction. Just as the Father performs the sacraments for his son, being prompted to it by the Injunction of begetting sons, which Injunction extends up to the final admonition addressed to the son (after Upanayana),тАФsimilarly the ┼Ъr─Бddha and other rites are performed, for the father by the son. Just as the maintaining of the living father is a necessary duty of the son, as laid down in (11.10A), so is it with the dead father also.

The performance of the act in question is not purely voluntary, like the Vai┼Ыv─Бnara sacrifice, in connection with which we readтАФтАШOn the birth of a son, one should offer the Vai┼Ыv─Бnara cake baked on twelve pans;тАФhe upon whose birth this offering is made becomes glorious, an enjoyer of food and endowed with efficient organs.тАЩ Here we find that the Father comes to perform the Yai┼Ыv─Бnara sacrifice when he desires certain results for his son; and it is not compulsory, like the Tonsure and other sacramental rites. As regards the act under consideration, on the other hand, we have the direction that тАШthe rite in honour of the Fathers should he performed till oneтАЩs death,тАЩ which shows that the rite is to be performed throughout oneтАЩs life.

As regards the objection that the result of the act, according to this view, does not accrue to the doer of the act,тАФthis is explained in a different manner: just as in the case of the Vai┼Ыv─Бnara sacrifice, the result, in the shape of having a highly qualified son, accrues to the father, who is the doer of the act,тАФso in the case in question also, the result, in the shape of the тАШFatherтАЩs satisfaction,тАЩ accrues to the son, the doer of the act. So that in both waysтАФwhether the result accrue to the father or to the performer of the rite,тАФthere is no incongruity at all. For as regards the father also, a result like the one in question is one that is desired by him in the very act of begetting the child; so that the father also does not obtain a reward not desired by him.

тАЬIf the ancestors are not the тАШdeitiesтАЩ of the ┼Ъr─Бddha-rite, how can it be called тАШpaitraтАЩ (in honour of ancestors), which term has been formed by the adding of the affix denoting the deity?тАЩтАЭ

What we say in answer to this is that the Fathers are regarded as deities on the ground of their being, like deities, the entities with reference to whom the offerings are made. The ancestors are referred to in some such form as тАШthis feeding of Br─Бhmaс╣Зas is done for the purpose of benefiting you.тАЩ In the offering called the тАШPiс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Э-Yaj├▒a,тАЩ the ancestors are actually тАШdeities but of ┼Ыr─Бddhas, the ancestors have not been regarded as тАШdeities.тАЩ As for this feeding of Br─Бhmaс╣Зas, it is on the same footing as the offerings tbat are made into the fire of portions of clarified butter, cake and such other things. And in this way the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas themselves occupy the position of ancestors. Hence at the time that the food is served to them, one should think of it being offered to his ancestors, with some such expression in his mindтАФтАШthis is offered to you, it is no longer mine.тАЩ The Br─Бhmaс╣Зas thus fed attain the position of the тАШ─Аhavan─лya fireтАЩ (into which libations are poured); the only difference being that into the ─Аhavan─лya the offering is actually thrown, while it is only placed near the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas, and they take it up themselves.

Nor will it be right to argue that тАЬ┼Ъr─Бddhas cannot be regarded as sacrifice, as in them the syllable тАШsv─Бh─БтАЩ is not pronounced with reference to the gods.тАЭ Because we find the same in the case of the тАШSviс╣гс╣нakс╣ЫtтАЩ offerings (which are regarded as sacrifice). Thus then, the ┼Ъr─Бdс╕Нha, even though of the nature of a тАШsacrifice,тАЩ can be offered to Ancestors. Nor is there any incongruity in the Ancestors being the тАШdeitiesтАЩ (of the offering) and also the recipients of the result. We are going to explain more about this matter, which is not directly mentioned in the text, under Chapter III.

From all this it becomes established that the Sun and the other gods arc not тАШdeitiesтАЩ in the feeding of Br─Бhmaс╣Зas.

тАЬThe definition of тАШdeityтАЩ as one who is aimed at in a sacrifice is too narrow; because as a matter of fact, we find the name тАШdeityтАЩ applied even in cases where there is no connection with any sacrifice; e.g., in such statements asтАФ(a) тАШthe worshipping of deities,тАЩ тАШone should approach the deities.тАЩ But neither worship, nor going forward (which is what is expressed by approaching), is possible with regard to deities.тАЭ

There is no force in this; as the worship may be taken as enjoined in connection with those cases where the deity is actually enjoined; or, it may refer to the deities as related to the Agnihotra and other sacrifices.

тАЬEven so, the difficulty does not cease. The deity can never be the object of worship; as that would deprive it of the very character of тАШDeityтАЩ (which has been defined as consisting in being aimed at in a sacrifice); for if it were the object of worship, it could not be the recipient of the sacrifice. It h as been declared that тАШthe active agent of one act cannot be an active agent of another.тАЩ The тАШactive agentтАЩ is a particular kind of force, and this force varies with each particular act; and as the presence of such force can be indicated only by its effects, we can reasonably assume only that much of diversity in it as there may be effects. From this it follows that what is the тАШrecipient of a giftтАЩ must remain the recipient, it cannot become the object.тАФтАШHow then do we have such expressions as give this to the cooker, where the nominative of the action of cooking becomes the recipient,тАФor having his body wounded by arrows, he went away helplessly, being looked upon by the glances of his beloved, [where the object of the act of looking becomes the nominative of the act of going ].тАЩтАФThe answer to this has already been explained:тАФsuch expressions become justified by the difference between the efficiency and the efficient being regarded as secondary and figurative; as is found to be the case in such expressions as тАШhaving eaten, he goes.тАЩ Thus then, if the aot in question is meant to be a worship, then its object cannot have the character of the тАШDeityтАЩ; while if the Sun and the rest are тАШdeities,тАЩ then the act enjoined cannot be regarded as тАШworship.тАЩ Nor can it be held that the Sun being well known as a тАШdeity,тАЩ the present injunction lays down its worship. Because the term тАШdeityтАЩ is not a common name of the Sun and other gods, in the way in which the term тАШgoтАЩ (cow) is of the тАШ┼ЫabaleyaтАЩ and other bovine varieties.тАЭ

To the above we make the following reply:тАФIt is quite true that the Sun and others are not, in their own form, тАШdeitiesтАЩ; the term тАШdeityтАЩ is a relative term; and it is only from an injunction that we can learn that a certain being is the тАШdeityтАЩ of an act; the fact being that when a certain offering is enjoined with reference to a being, this latter is the тАШdeityтАЩ of that offering. It is for this reason that Agni is not the тАШdeityтАЩ of any other offering save that тАШdedicated to Agni.тАЩ [All this is quite true] but no injunction of тАШworshipтАЩ is possible without the object to be worshipped; and deities are found to be mentioned as objects of worship. Now if the act of тАШworshipтАЩ is not possible when the term тАШdeityтАЩ is taken in its primary sense, then the тАШworshipтАЩ may be taken as being of the nature of тАШsacrifice.тАЩ But, in the absence of any mention (in the injunction of feeding Br─Бhmaс╣Зas) of the substance to be offered and the deity to whom it is to be offered, the act in question cannot acquire the character of true тАШsacrificeтАЩ; so that the text iu question may be regarded as a descriptive reference for the purpose of prescribing the тАШforenoonтАЩ as the proper time for it; the sense being that тАШall acts in honour of the gods should be done during the forenoon.тАЩ

тАЬWhy is it said that the deity is not directly mentioned?тАЭ

For the simple reason that there is no word directly signifying any deity. The term тАШdeityтАЩ that is actually found is the common name of all deities; so that the injunction refers to the worshipping of Agni, ─Аditya, Rudra, Indra, Viс╣гс╣Зu, Sarasvat─л and so forth; and during the worship there is offering of incense, light, garland, presents and such other things. In the case of Agni; the connection with the act of worship offered is always direct; as regards ─Аditya (the Sun-god) since he is far off, his worship consists in the placing of sandal-paste, flowers, etc., on a clean spot; and as regards Indra and the other gods, since they are not visible, their worshipping is done by the placing of flower, etc., accompanied by a reference to their names. Though in the act of worship, the beings worshipped form the predominant factor, yet inasmuch as they are subservient to the act to be done, it is the act of worship that comes to be recognised as what should be done. If the substance offered were the predominant factor, then the Deity could never form the subject of the injunction. All this is made clear in JaimimтАЩs M─лm─Бns─Б-S┼лtra, 2.1.6 and 7. The view put forward on the other hand is perfectly reasonable, the case being analogous to that of the Hymns and Eulogies. The Hymn is not made for the sake of the hymn itself; so the worship also is not for the sake of the worshipped. If might be argued that Hymns and Eulogies are not mentioned here by name. But the answer to this has already been given. The accusative has the sense of the instrumental, as in the expression тАШjuhoti,тАЩ where тАШsakt┼лnтАЩ has been taken as тАШsaktubhiс╕е.тАЩ

Similarly the sentence тАШmс╣Ыdam g─Бm daivatam pradakс╣гiс╣З─Бni kurv─лta,тАЩтАФтАШone should have the clay, the cow, the deity to his right,тАЩтАФlays down the use of the right hand; the sense being that all acts done in honour of the gods should be done with the right hand; the passage cannot mean that the deities ensouling the clay, etc., should be actually placed on the right; for the simple reason that the deities have no physical form.

The same holds good regarding the injunction тАШone should move up to the gods.тАЩ Since it is not possible for one to go near the gods by walking on foot, and since the root тАШgamтАЩ (as in тАШabhig─БccetтАЩ) signifies knowledge, why should тАШabhigamanaтАЩ differ from Remembrance? The sense thus is that during the act one should think of the gods; i.e., he should avoid all anxiety or distraction of the mind. In this way this Smrti is found to be one whose basis is actually found in the Vedic Injunction, which saysтАФтАШOne should think in his mind of that deity to whom he may be offering the libation.тАЩ

тАЬBut this thinking of the deity is already implied in the aiming (which has been put forward in the definition of the Deity),тАФwhich cannot be done without thinking.тАЭ

This objection has no force; as mere aiming can be done also by a man who is anxious and whose mind is distracted.

Thus then all suoс╕е expressions as тАШthe property of the gods,тАЩ тАШthe cattle of the gods,тАЩ тАШthe substance of the godsтАЩ and the like are to be taken as referring to such cattle and things as hare been assigned to (dedicated to) the gods. Some people have held that in the seotion dealing with penalties to be inflicted upon persons stealing the тАШproperty of gods,тАЩ it is the image of the god that is meant; as otherwise the regulations bearing upon the subject would become liable to he infringed. As regards the images upon whom the character of тАШgodsтАЩ has been imposed, things are called their тАШpropertyтАЩ on the basis of an assumed sense of ownership; and it is such property that is referred to as тАШproperty of the gods,тАЩ in such passages asтАФтАШthe highest penalty is to be inflicted on the stealing of the property of Gods, Br─Бhmaс╣Зas and Kings.тАЩ In reality, gods can have no rights of ownership; and hence the literal sense of the expression being inadmissible, it is only right that we should accept the figurative one.

тАЬIn the present case what is the figurative sense? In every instance of figurative use, the presenoe of a common function (or quality) forms the basis; e.g., the expression тАШthe Boy is FireтАЩ is used when the boy is found to possess the white resplendence of fire. Similarly in every case the figurative or secondary sense is recognised only where there is some common property present;тАФthe presence of suoс╕е property being cognised by means of perception and other means of cognition. In the case in question however, since the sense of the deity is recognisable only by the purpose served by it,тАФand the form of the deity cannot be ascertained through that purpose,тАФhow could there be any recognition of common properties?тАЭ

Our answer is as follows:тАФWe find particular forms of deities described in the Mantras and Arthav─Бdas; and all these descriptions are interpreted as figurative. People who do not perceive any basis for such interpretation take the passages in their literal sense and regard Indra and the deities as actually possessing those forms; and the similarity of such forms they actually perceive in the images; and in this sense also it is only natural that the description should he regarded as figurative.

Some people have explained that the feeding of Br─Бhmaс╣Зas at ┼Ъr─Бddha in honour of the Vi┼Ыvedevas is what is described here as being тАШin honour of the gods.тАЩ But such feeding, being part of what is done тАШin honour of ancestors,тАЩ becomes included under the latter phrase, and the re-iteration of it would he entirely meaningless. Then again, since we have the generic term тАШgods,тАЩ on what grounds could we restrict it to the Vi┼Ыvedevas only P If such restriction be based upon the association of the term тАШpitryaтАЩ тАШin honour of ancestors,тАЩтАФthen, since the acts thus spoken of would not he included in тАШthose done in honour of ancestors,тАЩтАФthe two words could he justified on the analogy of the expression тАШgo-balibarda,тАЩ тАШbovine bull,тАЩ which is used even when there is not much difference between what is denoted by the two terms.тАФ(189)

тАШс╣Ъс╣гivatтАЩтАФтАШLike an ascetic; i.e. avoiding honey, meat and other forbidden foodтАЩ (Medh─Бtithi and Kull┼лka);тАФтАШeating only a little wild-growing rice and other food fit for the asceticтАЩ (Govindar─Бja, N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa and Nandana).

Medh─Бtithi (p. 163, l. 17)тАФтАШMс╣Ыtasya kartс╣ЫtvamтАЩтАФThis refers to M─лm─Бс╣Гs─Б S┼лtra 10. 2. 55-56. рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The dutyтАФtbat one should eat the food given by one person only under certain circumstancesтАФthat has just been prescribed, is meant for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa only;тАФit has been so ordained тАШby the sagesтАЩтАФby the learned, after having learnt it from the Veda. They do not intend this to apply to the Kс╣гatriya and the Vai┼Ыya; which means that students belonging to these two castes should not eat any food except what they get as alms.

Objection.тАФтАЬAs a matter of fact, it is only the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa that is entitled to eat at ┼Ъr─Бddhas; as is clear from such declarations asтАФтАШWhich Brahmaс╣Зas are to be fed at ┼Ъr─Бddhaa, and which to be avoided?тАЩтАФтАШTo the most deserving Br─Бhamaс╣Зa etc.тАЩ and so forth; from which it is clear that the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa alone is entitled to receive gifts. Further, what we have here is a counter-exception, not an original Injunction; and all denials are dependent upon possibility [and in the present case there is, as just pointed out, no possibility of the feeding pertaining to any non-Br─Бhmaс╣Зa].тАЭ

To the above we make the following reply:тАФIt has been ordained that after the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas have eaten, the remnant should be disposed of by being made over to тАШrelationsтАЩ; and in this there is no restriction as to caste; the man thus would feed any one who may happen to be his тАШrelationтАЩ; and in this the recipients are indicated, not by the caste-names тАШKс╣гatriyaтАЩ etc., but simply by the general name тАШrelation.тАЩ It is in view of this possibility of non-Br─Бhmaс╣Зas partaking of the food at ┼Ъr─Бddhas that we have the prohibition in the Text.тАФ(190)

рдЕрдкреНрд░рдЪреЛрджрд┐рдд рдПрд╡ рд╡рд╛ ред

рдЖрдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╣рд┐рддреЗрд╖реБ рдЪ [рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдкрд╛рдардГ - рдЕрдзреНрдпрдпрдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧрдореН] рее реи.резрепрез рее

Prompted by the Teacher, or even when not prompted, he should put forth his exertion to study, and also to doing what is helpful to the teacher.тАФ(191)

рдиреЛрджрд┐рддреЛ94 рдЧреБрд░реБрдгрд╛рдирд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддреЛ рд╜рдкрд┐ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рджреН рдЕрдзреНрдпрдпрдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧрдВ рдпрддреНрдирдореН ред рдирдиреБ рдЪрд╛рд╣реВрддреЛ рд╜рдзреАрдпреАрдд рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЙрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдХрдердореН рдЕрдкреНрд░рдгреЛрджрд┐рддрд╕реНрдп рдпреЛрдЧ рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЧреГрд╣реАрддрд╡реЗрджреИрдХрджреЗрд╢рд╕реНрдп рдкрд░рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдХрдЧреБрдгрд╛рд░реНрдердореН рдПрддрджреН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рди рддрддреНрд░рд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд╜рдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдГ ред рдПрд╡рдореН рдЖрдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╛рдп рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рдпрджреН рдЙрджрдХреБрдореНрднрд╛рд╣рд░рдгрд╛рджрд┐ рд╢реНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрд╕рдВрд╡рд╛рд╣рдирд╛рджрд┐ рддрджреН рдЕрдкреНрдпреН рдЕрдирд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддреЗрди рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН рее реи.резрепрез рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШPromptedтАЩтАФorderedтАФтАШby the teacher, he put forth his exertionтАЩтАФmake an effortтАФтАШto study.тАЩ

тАЬIt has been already laid down that тАШone should rend when wanted by the Teacher.тАЩ How then can there he any exertion put forth by one who is not prompted?тАЭ

What is here said refers to the student who has learnt a part of the Veda, and is going to learn the remainder; for this latter the тАШinstruction of the teacherтАЩ is not necessary.

Similarly he should do, without being told to do so, such helpful acts for the teacher as fetching jars of water, massaging his body whenever he happens to be fatigued, and so forth.тАФ(191)

рдХреБрддрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рджреН рдЖрдЧрддреЛ рдЧреБрд░реЛрд░реН рдореБрдЦрдВ рд╡реАрдХреНрд╖рдорд╛рдгрд╕реН рддрд┐рд╖реНрдареЗрдиреН рдиреЛрдкрд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрддреН ред рдирд┐рдпрдореНрдп рдЪ рд╢рд░реАрд░рдВ ред рдкрд╛рджрд╣рд╕реНрддрдЪрд╛рд▓рдирд╣рд╕рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ рди рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН, рди рдХрд┐рдВрдЪрд┐рджреН рд╡рджреЗрддреН, рдЕрдиреБрдкрдпреЛрдЧрд┐ ред рдмреБрджреНрдзреАрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдгрд┐ рдирд┐рдпрдЪреНрдЫреЗрддреН ред рдпрджреН рдЖрд╢реНрдЪрд░реНрдпрд░реВрдкрдВ рдХрд┐рдВрдЪрд┐рджреН рдЧреБрд░реБрд╕рдХрд╛рд╢реЗ рди рддрддреН рдкреБрдирдГ рдкреБрдирд░реН рднрд╛рд╡рдпреЗрддреН ред рд╢реНрд░реЛрддреНрд░рд╛рджреАрдиреНрдпреН рдЕрдкрд┐ ред рдЪрдХреНрд╖реБрд░реНрдирд┐рдпрдорд╕реН рддреБ рдЧреБрд░реБрд╡рдХреНрддреНрд░рдкреНрд░реЗрдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджреН рдПрд╡ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдГ ред рдордирд╢реН рдЪ рдирд┐рдпрдЪреНрдЫреЗрдЪреН рдЫрд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдпрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рдХрд▓реНрдкрд╛рдиреН рдЧреГрд╣рдХреБрд╢реВрд▓рд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рд░рдореНрднрд╛рдиреН рдордирд╕рд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдЬрдпреЗрддреН ред рдЙрдХреНрддрд╕реН рддреБ “рд╕рдВрдпрдореЗ рдпрддреНрдирдореН” (рдореНрдзреН реи.реорео) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдХреНрддрд┐рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрд╛рд░реНрдердГ95 рд╕ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрдГ ред рдЧреБрд░реБрд╕рдВрдирд┐рдзреМ рд╕реНрд╡рд▓реНрдкреЛ рд╜рдкреАрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдореН рдЕрдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖рд┐рджреНрдзреЗ рд╜рдкрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд░реЛ рди рджреЗрдпрдГ ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЮреНрдЬрд▓рд┐рд░реН рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рдХреГрддрдХрд░рдХрдкреЛрддрдГ рее реи.резрепреи рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

On coming from some other place, тАШhe should stand looking at the face of his Teacher,тАЩтАФhe should not sit;тАФтАШhaving under control, his bodyтАЩ;тАФi.e., he should not do such acts as the throwing about of hands and feet, laughing and so forth; nor should he speak anything needlessly.

He should control his тАШorgans of sensation,тАЩтАФi.e, if he finds anything wonderful near the Teacher, he should not think of it again and again. He should control the Auditory and other organs also; the control of the visual organ is secured by looking at the TeacherтАЩs face.

He should control the mind also; i.e., he should avoid the thought of difficulties pertaining to soriptural matters, or of the building of houses, granaries and the like.

The prohibition contained under 288 with regard to тАШmaking an effort to control, etc.,тАЩтАФis meant to prohibit attachment.

The meaning of all this is that when he is near his Teacher, he should not permit the slightest movement of his organs, even towards such things as are not prohibited.

тАШWith joined palmтАЩтАФi.e., with the hands joined together in the shape of a pigeon, turned upwards.тАФ(192)

Gautama (1-52, 53).тАФтАШCatching hold of the left hand, leaving the thumb free, he should request the teacher with the words, Teach, Sir;тАФfixing his eyes and mind thereon.тАЩ
